## PAGE 00001: (2026x Refresh1) Adding projects to the server

- page_id: `304014989`
- space_key: `SYSML2CM`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/SYSML2CM/pages/304014989/2026x+Refresh1+Adding+projects+to+the+server
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-04-29T17:17:40.409+02:00`
- ancestors: Versions of SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

#### NOTE: Prerequisites

Prerequisites

To add projects to the server, you must have the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Permissions' space='MCS'] or the Resource Creator role for the category in which you want to store projects.

You can add projects to the server in one of the following ways:

- 
- 

##### Creating server projects

To create a server project

1. Do one of the following to open the New Server Project dialog:
  - In the main menu, select Collaborate > New Server Project .
  - In the main menu, select Collaborate > Projects and click the New button. [ATTACHMENT filename='new_server_project.png']
2. On the left side of the dialog, select the SysML v2 Project type.
3. In the Name box, enter the project name.
4. Optionally, click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] next to the **Category**box, and select the category where you want to store your project. To create a new category for the project, click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] in the **Select Category** dialog.
5. Click OK .

##### Importing local projects to the server

To import a local project to the server

1. Open the project you want to add to the server from the local repository.
2. In the main menu, select Collaborate > Add Project to Server . Only projects saved as new versions can be added to the server. If your local project is saved as a draft, you will be prompted to save it as a new version before proceeding to the next step. For more information, see the *Saving local projects* section on page [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Managing local projects' space='SYSML2P']
3. In the Import Project to the Server dialog, review the actions that will be performed on the main project and any used projects. [ATTACHMENT filename='import_project_to_server_dialog.png']
4. Optionally, click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] next to the **Category**box, and select the category where you want to store your project. To create a new category for the project, click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] in the **Select Category** dialog. Click the Import button.

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=304015004 space=SYSML2CM version=1 -->
## PAGE 00002: (2026x Refresh1) Branching projects

- page_id: `304015004`
- space_key: `SYSML2CM`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/SYSML2CM/pages/304015004/2026x+Refresh1+Branching+projects
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-04-29T17:17:40.626+02:00`
- ancestors: Versions of SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) Managing server projects
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

Creating a project branch duplicates a specific project version and enables users to work on the project simultaneously. Branching increases productivity if several development teams are working on a single product. Branches can be created from any version/iteration of a project or its branch. The branch holds the information about the project version/iteration it is derived from.

#### NOTE: Permissions

Permissions

To create, remove, rename, archive, or unarchive a branch in Teamwork Cloud, you must have the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Permissions' space='MCS'].

##### Creating project branches

To create a project branch

1. In the main menu, select Collaborate > Projects .
2. In the Manage Projects dialog, select the project you want to branch and click [ATTACHMENT filename='select_branch.png'] .
3. In the Select Branch dialog, click the Edit Branches button.
4. In the Edit Branches dialog, select the project version/iteration you want to branch and click the Create Branch button. [ATTACHMENT filename='edit_branches_dialog.png']
5. In the Branch name box of the open dialog, enter the branch name.
6. In the Comment box, optionally enter the branch description.
7. (For Teamwork Cloud only). If you want to branch project usages together with the main project, select the Branch used projects check box. [ATTACHMENT filename='create_branch_dialog.png']
8. Click OK . A new branch is created and displayed in the Edit Branches dialog. [ATTACHMENT filename='displaying_created_branch.png']

##### Opening project branches

To open a project branch

1. In the main menu, select Collaborate > Projects .
2. In the Manage Projects dialog, select the project whose branch you want to open and click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] .
3. In the **Select Branch** dialog, select the desired project branch and click **OK**. You can see the selected branch in the **Branch** column of the **Manage Projects** dialog.
4. Click the Open button to open the project branch.

The selected branch is displayed in the **Manage Projects** dialog. The branch name is displayed in the **Branch** column and you can open it as any other project.

##### Archiving project branches

You can hide the project branches that you do not work with anymore and maintain only for historical purposes.

To archive a project branch

1. In the main menu, select Collaborate > Projects .
2. In the Manage Projects dialog, s elect the project whose branch you want to archive and click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] .
3. In the Select Branch dialog, click the Edit Branches button.
4. In the Edit Branches dialog, r ight-click the branch you want to archive and select **Mark as Archived**. 
**[IMAGE alt='' src='']**

By default, archived branches are hidden in the project version tree.

- To show/hide archived branches, click [ATTACHMENT filename='options_button.png'] in the Edit Branches or Select Branch dialog and select or deselect the Show Archived Branches command.
- To unarchive an archived branch, right-click the archived branch in the Edit Branches dialog and deselect the **Mark as Archived** command.

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=304015046 space=SYSML2CM version=1 -->
## PAGE 00003: (2026x Refresh1) Changing used project versions or iterations

- page_id: `304015046`
- space_key: `SYSML2CM`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/SYSML2CM/pages/304015046/2026x+Refresh1+Changing+used+project+versions+or+iterations
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-04-29T17:17:41.252+02:00`
- ancestors: Versions of SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) Working with used projects
- labels: ['unrestored-unknown-attachment']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

When a new version/iteration of a used project becomes available on the server, you may want to change the used project version/iteration in your main project to the latest one.

#### NOTE: Permissions

Permissions

To change the used project version in Teamwork Cloud, you must have:

- Read Resources, Edit Resources, Edit Resource Properties, and Administer Resources permissions for the main project
- Read Resources permission for the used project.

##### Changing used project versions

The quickest way to change the used project version is via the Containment tree, but you can also use the **Project Usages** dialog.

To change the used project version via the Containment tree

1. In the Containment tree of the main project, expand the Used Projects node.
2. Right-click a used project and select Change Version . [ATTACHMENT filename='changing_used_project_version_via_containment_tree.png']
3. In the Edit Branches dialog, select a new used project version/iteration and click OK .

To change the used project version/iteration via the **Project Usages** dialog

1. Open the Project Usages dialog:
  - In the main menu, select Options > Project Usages .
  - In the main menu, select Collaborate > Project Usages > Project Usages .
2. Do one of the following:
  - Select a used project and click [ATTACHMENT filename='select_branch.png'] .
  - Right-click a used project and select Change Version / Change Iteration . [IMAGE alt='' src='']
3. In the Edit Branches dialog, select a new used project version/iteration and click OK .

You can check the version of a used project after selecting it in the **Project Usages** dialog. Versions/iterations are displayed in the following format:*#<used version/iteration>/<latest version/iteration>.*

##### Updating used projects to the latest version

To update the used project version/iteration

1. Open the Project Usages dialog:
  - In the main menu, select Options > Project Usages .
  - In the main menu, select Collaborate > Project Usages > Project Usages .
2. Click [ATTACHMENT filename='update_used_projects.png'] .
3. In the Update Used Projects dialog, select the projects you want to update and click OK . If a used project is configured to show notifications about new versions with specific tags, only the versions meeting the notification criteria are displayed in this dialog. [ATTACHMENT filename='update_used_projects_dialog.png']

##### Configuring notifications about new used project versions

###### Changing notification settings for all used projects

By default, you will get a notification aboutnew used project versions every time you open the main project. You can change the setting for these notifications in the **Environment Options** dialog.

To change the notification settings for all used projects

1. In the main menu, select **Options** > **Environment**.
2. In the **Environment Options** dialog, select the**Collaboration** option group.
3. Change the value of the **Notify About Newer Project Usages**option, to one of the following:
  - Open - to show notifications about new used project versions every time you open the main project.
  - Open, Update - to show notifications about new used project versions every time you open or update the main project.
  - **Never** - to disable notifications about new used project versions.
4. Click **OK** to close the **Environment Options** dialog.

###### Getting notifications about new versions of a specific used project (Teamwork Cloud only)

If you work with Teamwork Cloud, you can choose to get notifications about all new versions of a specific used project.

To get notifications about new versions of a specific used project (Teamwork Cloud only)

1. Open the Project Usages dialog:
  - In the main menu, select Options > Project Usages .
  - In the main menu, select Collaborate > Project Usages > Project Usages .
2. Select the used project you want to get notifications about.
3. On the right side of the dialog, select the check box next to the Notify on drop-down box.
4. In the drop-down box, select **Notify for Any New Version**. 
 
[IMAGE alt='' src='']
5. Click **OK** to close the **Project Usages** dialog.

###### Getting notifications about new used project versions with specific tags (Teamwork Cloud only)

If you work with Teamwork Cloud, you can choose to get notifications about new versions of the selected used project with specific version tags.

To get notifications about new used project versions with specific tags (Teamwork Cloud only)

1. Open the Project Usages dialog:
  - In the main menu, select Options > Project Usages .
  - In the main menu, select Collaborate > Project Usages > Project Usages .
2. Select the used project you want to get notifications about.
3. On the right side of the dialog, select the check box next to the Notify on drop-down box.
4. In the drop-down box, select **New Tagged Version**.
5. Click the **Specify Tags**, link highlighted in the below figure. 
 
[IMAGE alt='' src='']
6. In the **Specify Tags**dialog, enter a version tag and click [IMAGE alt='' src='']. The tag is added to the tag list. 
 
[IMAGE alt='' src='']
7. If needed, repeat the previous step to add more tags. To remove a tag, select the tag in the **Specify Tags** dialog and click [IMAGE alt='' src=''].
8. Click OK to close the Specify Tags dialog.

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

Versions/iterations are displayed in the following format:<em> #&lt;used version/iteration&gt;/&lt;latest version/iteration&gt;.</em></p><h3>Updating used projects to the latest version</h3><p>To update the used project version/iteration</p><hr /><ol><li>Open the <strong>Project Usages</strong> dialog:<ul><li>In the main menu, select <strong>Options</strong> &gt; <strong>Project Usages</strong>.</li><li>In the main menu, select <strong>Collaborate</strong> &gt; <strong>Project Usages</strong> &gt; <strong>Project Usages</strong>.</li></ul></li><li>Click <ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="update_used_projects.png"><ri:page ri:content-title="(2026x Refresh1) Changing used project versions or iterations" /></ri:attachment></ac:image>.</li><li>In the <strong>Update Used Projects</strong> dialog, select the projects you want to update and click <strong>OK</strong>.<br /><ac:structured-macro ac:name="note" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="7fecea2e-6376-4854-a218-62617c82e1d1"><ac:rich-text-body><p><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">If a used project is configured to show notifications about new versions with specific tags, only the versions meeting the notification criteria are displayed in this dialog.</span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><br /><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="update_used_projects_dialog.png"><ri:page ri:content-title="(2026x Refresh1) Changing used project versions or iterations" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></li></ol><h3>Configuring notifications about new used project versions</h3><h4>Changing notification settings for all used projects</h4><p>By default, you will get a notification about<span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"> new used project versions every time you open the main project. You can change the setting for these notifications in the <strong>Environment Options</strong> dialog.</span></p><p><br /></p><p>To change the notification settings for all used projects</p><hr /><ol><li><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">In the main menu, select <strong>Options</strong> &gt; <strong>Environment</strong>.</span></li><li><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">In the <strong>Environment Options</strong> dialog, select the<strong> Collaboration</strong> option group.</span></li><li><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">Change the value of the <strong>Notify About Newer Project Usages </strong>option, to one of the following:</span><ul><li><strong>Open</strong> - to show notifications about new used project versions every time you open the main project.</li><li><strong>Open, Update</strong> - to show notifications about new used project versions every time you open or update the main project.</li><li><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"><strong>Never</strong> - to disable notifications about new used project versions.</span></li></ul></li><li><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">Click <strong>OK</strong> to close the <strong>Environment Options</strong> dialog.</span></li></ol><h4><span>Getting notifications about new versions of a specific used project (Teamwork Cloud only)</span></h4><p><span>If you work with Teamwork Cloud, you can choose to get notifications about all new versions of a specific used project.</span></p><p><br /></p><p>To get notifications about new versions of a specific used project (Teamwork Cloud only)</p><hr /><ol><li>Open the <strong>Project Usages</strong> dialog:<ul><li>In the main menu, select <strong>Options</strong> &gt; <strong>Project Usages</strong>.</li><li>In the main menu, select <strong>Collaborate</strong> &gt; <strong>Project Usages</strong> &gt; <strong>Project Usages</strong>.</li></ul></li><li><span>Select the used project you want to get notifications about.</span></li><li>On the right side of the dialog, select the check box next to the <strong>Notify on</strong> drop-down box.</li><li><span>In the drop-down box, select <strong>Notify for Any New Version</strong>.<br /><br /><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="any_new_version.png"><ri:page ri:content-title="(2026x Refresh1) Changing used project versions or iterations" /></ri:attachment></ac:image><br /><br /></span></li><li><span>Click <strong>OK</strong> to close the <strong>Project Usages</strong> dialog. </span></li></ol><h4>Getting notifications about new used project versions with specific tags (Teamwork Cloud only)</h4><p><span style="font-weight: 400;letter-spacing: 0.0px;">If you work with Teamwork Cloud, you can choose to get notifications about new versions of the selected used project with specific version tags.</span></p><p><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"> </span></p><p><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">To get notifications about new used project versions with specific tags (Teamwork Cloud only)</span></p><hr /><ol><li>Open the <strong>Project Usages</strong> dialog:<ul><li>In the main menu, select <strong>Options</strong> &gt; <strong>Project Usages</strong>.</li><li>In the main menu, select <strong>Collaborate</strong> &gt; <strong>Project Usages</strong> &gt; <strong>Project Usages</strong>.</li></ul></li><li><span>Select the used project you want to get notifications about.</span></li><li>On the right side of the dialog, select the check box next to the <strong>Notify on</strong> drop-down box.</li><li><span>In the drop-down box, select <strong>New Tagged Version</strong>.</span></li><li><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">Click the <strong>Specify Tags</strong>, link highlighted in the below figure.<br /><br /><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="notifications_about_new_tagged_versions.png"><ri:page ri:content-title="(2026x Refresh1) Changing used project versions or iterations" /></ri:attachment></ac:image><br /><br /></span></li><li><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">In the <strong>Specify Tags </strong>dialog, enter a version tag and click <ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="add_value.png"><ri:page ri:content-title="(2026x Refresh1) Changing used project versions or iterations" /></ri:attachment></ac:image>. The tag is added to the tag list.<br /><br /><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="specify_tags.png"><ri:page ri:content-title="(2026x Refresh1) Changing used project versions or iterations" /></ri:attachment></ac:image><br /><br /></span></li><li><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">If needed, repeat the previous step to add more tags.<br /></span><ac:structured-macro ac:name="note" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="c845a451-ca65-4ba4-8c60-217564e96ff6"><ac:rich-text-body><p>To remove a tag, select the tag in the <strong>Specify Tags</strong> dialog and click <ac:image ac:thumbnail="true" ac:height="16"><ri:attachment ri:filename="remove_value.png"><ri:page ri:content-title="(2026x Refresh1) Changing used project versions or iterations" /></ri:attachment></ac:image>.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></li><li>Click <strong>OK</strong> to close the <strong>Specify Tags</strong> dialog.</li></ol>
````

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=304015115 space=SYSML2CM version=1 -->
## PAGE 00004: (2026x Refresh1) Committing changes to the server

- page_id: `304015115`
- space_key: `SYSML2CM`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/SYSML2CM/pages/304015115/2026x+Refresh1+Committing+changes+to+the+server
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-04-29T17:17:42.495+02:00`
- ancestors: Versions of SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

After you finish editing a model, you need to commit the changes to the server so that other team members can see these changes when editing other parts of the model. When you commit changes to the server, new data from your modeling tool is merged with the project on the server. As a result, a new version/iteration of that project is created. Other team members must [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='(2026x Refresh1) Updating changes from the server' space=''] from the server to see the committed changes.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### The workflow of modifying and committing server projects.

##### Committing changes

To commit a project to the server

1. In the main menu, select Collaborate > Commit Changes To Server (or press Ctrl+K).
2. If you want to describe the changes you made, enter a comment in the **Comment** box of the **Commit Changes to the Server**dialog. Click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] above the **Comment** box to choose a comment from the recently used comments list. [ATTACHMENT filename='commit_project_to_the _server_dialog.png']
3. Optionally, click More in the lower left corner of the dialog and do the following:
  - .
  - .
4. Click the Commit button.

While the project is being committed, you will see a dialog with a progress bar and your position in the commit queue as shown below.

When multiple projects are committed to the server simultaneously, all users are put in a First-In-First-Out (FIFO) line resulting in quicker and more predictable project commit execution. If putting project commits in a queue does not work for your organization, your system administrator can for a particular Teamwork Cloud server.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### The commit progress dialog with your position in the commit queue.

##### Creating version tags

You can create tags for a Teamwork Cloud project version when you commit it to the server. Version tags provide valuable information when [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='(2026x Refresh1) Reviewing project history' space=''] or [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='(2026x Refresh1) Branching projects' space='']. You can also use tags to trigger notifications when used project versions with specific tags are committed to the server. To learn more, see [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='(2026x Refresh1) Changing used project versions or iterations' space=''].

To commit a project with a version tag

1. In the main menu. select Collaborate > Commit Changes To Server (or press Ctrl+K).
2. In the lower left corner of the Commit Changes to the Server dialog, click More .
3. In the Version Tags tab, click the Add button.
4. In the open dialog, type the tag text and click OK . The tag is added to the Version Tags tab. You create several tags for one project version.Select the **Create major version** check box, to add the 'Major' tag to the project version. [ATTACHMENT filename='creating_version_tag.png']
5. Click the Commit button.

##### Reviewing local changes before committing a project

You can review the local changes you have made to the project before committing it to the server.

To review local changes and commit a project

1. In the main menu. select Collaborate > Commit Changes To Server (or press Ctrl+K).
2. In the lower left corner of the Commit Changes to the Server dialog, click More .
3. Select the Local Changes tab and review local changes made to the project. Added elements are highlighted in green, deleted elements are highlighted in red, and modified or moved elements are highlighted in blue. [ATTACHMENT filename='reviewing_local_changes.png']
4. Click the Commit button.

##### Disabling commit queues

If putting project commits in a First-In-First-Out (FIFO) line does not work for your organization, your system administrator candisable the commit queue mechanismfor a particular Teamwork Cloud server.

To disable commit queues

1. Open for editing the <install_root>/TeamworkCloud/configuration/application.conf file.
2. Add the following line to the file:
3. Restart the Teamwork Cloud server.

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=304015159 space=SYSML2CM version=1 -->
## PAGE 00005: (2026x Refresh1) Creating and managing categories

- page_id: `304015159`
- space_key: `SYSML2CM`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/SYSML2CM/pages/304015159/2026x+Refresh1+Creating+and+managing+categories
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-04-29T17:17:43.592+02:00`
- ancestors: Versions of SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) Managing server projects
- labels: ['unrestored-unknown-attachment']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

You can organize the project repository by creating categories and grouping projects within them. By default, there is a single category named *Uncategorized*, but you can create as many categories as you need. The server supports a hierarchical category structure, allowing you to nest categories. Categories can be renamed and removed. In addition, you can move projects from one category to another.

#### NOTE: Teamwork Cloud permissions

Teamwork Cloud permissions

- To create categories, you must have the Manage Categories permission.
- Project categories are visible only if you have the Manage Categories permission or the Read Resources permission for at least one project within a category.

Creating categories

To create a category

1. In the main menu, select Collaborate > Projects .
2. In the Manage Projects dialog, do one of the following:
  - Select a category and click [ATTACHMENT filename='create_category_button.png'] .
  - Right-click a category and select Create Category .
3. In the **Create Category** dialog, optionally change the parent category by clicking [IMAGE alt='' src=''] next to the **Parent** box.
4. In the Name box, enter the category name. [ATTACHMENT filename='create_category_dialog.png']
5. Click OK .

##### Renaming categories

To rename a category

1. In the main menu, select Collaborate > Projects .
2. In the Manage Projects dialog, do one of the following:
  - Select a category and click [ATTACHMENT filename='rename_category.png'] .
  - Right-click a category and select Rename Category .
3. In the Name box of the Rename Category dialog, enter a new category name. [ATTACHMENT filename='rename_category_dialog.png']
4. Click OK .

##### Moving projects

To move a project to another category

1. In the main menu, select Collaborate > Projects .
2. In the Manage Projects dialog, do one of the following:
  - Select the project you and click [ATTACHMENT filename='move_to_category.png'] .
  - Right-click a project and select Move to Category .
3. In the Move to Category dialog, select the category you want to move the project to. If you want to move a project to a new category, click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] and create a new category.
4. Click OK .

##### Removing categories

#### NOTE: Teamwork Cloud permissions

Teamwork Cloud permissions

- You need to have the Manage Resources permission to delete a category.
- You need to have the Read Resources and Remove Resources permissions to delete all the resources within a category.

To remove a category

1. In the main menu, select Collaborate > Projects .
2. In the Manage Projects dialog, do one of the following:
  - Select a category and click [ATTACHMENT filename='delete_category.png'] .
  - Right-click a category and select Delete Category .
3. In the question dialog, click Yes to confirm your decision.

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

category.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></li><li>Click <strong>OK</strong>.</li></ol><h3>Removing categories</h3><ac:structured-macro ac:name="note" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="2c8eabe0-d3a0-4972-8f66-37a8b85f1a7f"><ac:parameter ac:name="title">Teamwork Cloud permissions</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><ul><li>You need to have the Manage Resources permission to delete a category.</li><li>You need to have the Read Resources and Remove Resources permissions to delete all the resources within a category.</li></ul></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><p><br /></p><p>To remove a category</p><hr /><ol><li>In the main menu, select <strong>Collaborate</strong> &gt; <strong>Projects</strong>.</li><li>In the <strong>Manage Projects</strong> dialog, do one of the following:<ul><li>Select a category and click <ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="delete_category.png"><ri:page ri:content-title="(2026x Refresh1) Creating and managing categories" /></ri:attachment></ac:image>.</li><li>Right-click a category and select <strong>Delete Category</strong>.</li></ul></li><li>In the question dialog, click <strong>Yes</strong> to confirm your decision.</li></ol>
````

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=304015180 space=SYSML2CM version=1 -->
## PAGE 00006: (2026x Refresh1) Creating indexing configuration for SysML v2 API Querying

- page_id: `304015180`
- space_key: `SYSML2CM`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/SYSML2CM/pages/304015180/2026x+Refresh1+Creating+indexing+configuration+for+SysML+v2+API+Querying
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-04-29T17:17:44.446+02:00`
- ancestors: Versions of SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) Server-side capabilities
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

For SysML v2 API Query Services to support queries that include derived properties, the SysML v2 resources to be queried must be indexed in advance.

This chapter describes how to index selected SysML v2 resources to get the most out of the SysML v2 standard API.

#### NOTE: Prerequisites

Prerequisites

- To enable this functionality, you need to [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Global element usage indexing and search' space='MCS'] .
- Only users with [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='User roles and permissions' space='MCS'] can create indexing configurations.

To create SysML v2 API Querying indexing configurations

1. In the right-side menu of the Settings application, select **Indexing management**.
2. Select tab **SysML v2 API Querying******at the top.
3. Click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] on the bottom right corner of the screen as shown in the figure above.
4. In the open wizard, make sure that the indexing configuration type **SysML v2 API Querying** is selected.
5. Select the resource you want to create an indexing configuration for and click **Next**. NoteYou can index only one resource at a time. Note that only indexed resources can be queried.
6. In the last step of the wizard, select one of the following indexing modes:
  - Automatic (default) - the resource is automatically indexed every time new project versions are committed in the indexing scope.
  - Manual - the resource is indexed only when indexing is initiated by an authorized user.
  - By specific commit tag - the resource is indexed only when new project versions are committed with a specified commit tag in the indexing scope. If you select this indexing mode, the Commit tag box appears where you need to specify the desired commit tag. [ATTACHMENT filename='indexing_sysml2.png']
7. Click the Create button.

The created indexing configuration automatically appears in the Indexing configurations list on the SysML v2 API Querying tab. To refresh the indexing status, reload the web page.

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

## PAGE 00007: (2026x Refresh1) Editing used projects

- page_id: `304015038`
- space_key: `SYSML2CM`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/SYSML2CM/pages/304015038/2026x+Refresh1+Editing+used+projects
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-04-29T17:17:41.036+02:00`
- ancestors: Versions of SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) Working with used projects
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

Server projects can only use other projects in read-only mode. To edit a used project, you must open it as stand-alone.

To open a used project for editing

1. In the Containment tree of the main project, expand the Used Projects node.
2. Right-click a used project and select one of the following: Note that the used project version/iteration is not updated after editing the used project. [ATTACHMENT filename='opening_used_project.png']
  - Open This Version - to open the used project version that the main project currently uses. If the used project version is not the latest one, the project will open in read-only mode.
  - **Open Latest Version** - to open the latest version of the used project for editing.

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=304015173 space=SYSML2CM version=2 -->
## PAGE 00009: (2026x Refresh1) Managing Standard Libraries

- page_id: `304015173`
- space_key: `SYSML2CM`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/SYSML2CM/pages/304015173/2026x+Refresh1+Managing+Standard+Libraries
- version_number: 2
- version_date: `2026-04-29T17:18:39.074+02:00`
- ancestors: Versions of SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) Managing server projects
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

A new Teamwork Cloud installation comes with an empty predefined **Standard Libraries**category. Below are tips for managing this category:

- When you add the very first SysML v2 project to the server, this category gets populated with 3DS-provided standard SysML v2 libraries (3DS SysML Customization and Standard Libraries). A set of version-specific (e.g., 2026x) Standard Libraries is added to the category only once during initial SysML v2 project creation.
- To add a SysML v2 Standard Library to the Standard Libraries category, you need the Create Resource permission (Resource Creator role with the Standard Libraries category scope).
- As new modeling tool versions are released, new version libraries are added to the version-specific branch of an already existing Standard Libraries resource. This requires the Administer Resources permission (Resource Manager role). Important note on rolesDo not assign the Resource Creator or Resource Manager roles for the predefined category indiscriminately. These roles should be granted only to users responsible for introducing initial SysML v2 capabilities on the server side and to those responsible for upgrading modeling tool versions (including uploading new versions of the Standard Libraries). The automatically assigned Resource Reviewer role is sufficient for all routine SysML v2 modeling activities.
- Non-standard SysML v2 projects cannot be added to the Standard Libraries category.
- The Standard Libraries category cannot be renamed or removed.
- You cannot successfully open a SysML v2 project without resolving the references to the standard libraries in the category. Therefore, each Teamwork Cloud user gets assigned the Read Resource permission through a scoped Resource Reviewer role by default.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### The *Standard Libraries* package of a SysML v2 project.

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=304015076 space=SYSML2CM version=1 -->
## PAGE 00010: (2026x Refresh1) Offline modeling

- page_id: `304015076`
- space_key: `SYSML2CM`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/SYSML2CM/pages/304015076/2026x+Refresh1+Offline+modeling
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-04-29T17:17:41.665+02:00`
- ancestors: Versions of SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation
- labels: ['offline-project', 'offline-projects', 'update-offline-project']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

Server projects support offline modeling which allows you to:

- Work with projects when connection to the server is not available.
- Save intermediate changes locally and commit changes to the server later.
- Save time as saving changes locally is much quicker than committing them to the server.

In an offline project, you can:

- Edit model elements.
- Create new model elements and diagrams.
- Review project structure (used projects), project options, and styles.
- Save changes locally.

When the connection to the server is established, you can commit and/or update project changes.

##### Making projects available offline

To make a server project available offline

1. Open a server project.
2. In the main menu, select one of the following:
  - Collaborate > Saves Changes Locally / Make Available Offline .
  - File > Save Project .

Once a server project is available offline you can find it in the **Offline Projects** tab of the **Open Server Project** and **Manage Projects** dialogs. When you open an offline project, the modeling tool title bar will display "Available Offline" after the project information.

An offline project is not a local copy of a server project!

Offline projects are saved in a restricted folder of the user home directory, e.g. *<disk_name>\Users\<user_name>\AppData\Local\<modeling_tool_name>\<modeling_tool_version>\restricted*. Offline projects are saved as multiple files in different folders, unlike regular local projects. You can open offline projects only by using a modeling tool.

##### Opening offline projects

To open an offline project

1. Do one of the following:
  - In the main menu, select Collaborate > Open Server Project .
  - Press Ctrl+Shift+O
2. In the Open Server Project dialog, select the Offline Projects tab.
3. Select the offline project you want to open and click OK . [ATTACHMENT filename='opening_offline_project.png']

##### Updating offline projects after load

You can choose to update an offline project after each load if the connection to the server is available.

To update an offline project after loading

1. Do one of the following:
  - In the main menu, select Collaborate > Open Server Project .
  - Press Ctrl+Shift+O
2. In the Open Server Project dialog, select the Offline Projects tab.
3. Right-click an offline project and select Update Project After Load . [ATTACHMENT filename='updating_project_after_load.png']

The option to update an offline project after load remains selected after reloading the project.

##### Removing offline projects

To stop using the offline project version, you need to remove it. This action does not remove a project from the server; it only removes the offline project version from your local machine.

Online Projects

Open Server Project

Open From Server

To remove an offline project

1. In the main menu, select Collaborate > Projects .
2. In the Manage Projects dialog, select the Offline Projects tab.
3. Select an offline project you want to remove and click the Remove button.

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

````html

In this case, uncommitted changes made to the offline project will be lost. </ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><p><span> <br /></span></p><p>To remove an offline project</p><hr /><ol><li>In the main menu, select <strong>Collaborate</strong> &gt; <strong>Projects</strong>.</li><li>In the <strong>Manage Projects</strong> dialog, select the <strong>Offline Projects</strong> tab. </li><li>Select an offline project you want to remove and click the <strong>Remove</strong> button.</li></ol>
````

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=304015143 space=SYSML2CM version=1 -->
## PAGE 00011: (2026x Refresh1) Opening server projects

- page_id: `304015143`
- space_key: `SYSML2CM`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/SYSML2CM/pages/304015143/2026x+Refresh1+Opening+server+projects
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-04-29T17:17:43.074+02:00`
- ancestors: Versions of SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation
- labels: ['unrestored-unknown-attachment']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

To start working with a server project, [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='(2026x Refresh1) Starting a collaboration session' space=''] and open the project as described below.

To open a server project

1. Do one of the following:
  - In the main menu, select Collaborate > Open Server Project .
  - Press Ctrl+Shift+O
2. In the Online Projects tab of the open dialog, select the project you want to open. [ATTACHMENT filename='open_server_project_dialog.png']
3. Click the Open button. You may be prompted to enter a password if the selected project is [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='(2026x Refresh1) Password-protected projects' space=''].If a project is available offline (displayed in the**Offline****Projects**tab), the offline project version will open even if you choose to open the project from the**Online Projects**tab. This mechanism ensures that the changes made to the offline project version are not lost. For more information, see[CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='(2026x Refresh1) Offline modeling' space='']. To open such a project from the server, right-click the project and select **Open From Server**.

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=304015065 space=SYSML2CM version=1 -->
## PAGE 00012: (2026x Refresh1) Password-protected projects

- page_id: `304015065`
- space_key: `SYSML2CM`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/SYSML2CM/pages/304015065/2026x+Refresh1+Password-protected+projects
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-04-29T17:17:41.496+02:00`
- ancestors: Versions of SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) Managing server projects
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

You can protect server projects with a password. The password protects all project versions.

#### NOTE: Prerequisites

Prerequisites

To set, update, and remove project passwords, you need the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Permissions' space='MCS'].

##### Setting a project password

To set a project password

1. In the main menu, select Collaborate > Projects .
2. In the Manage Projects dialog, do one of the following:
  - Select a project and click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] .
  - Right-click a project and select Set Password . [ATTACHMENT filename='setting_project_password.png']
3. In the Set Password dialog, enter and confirm the project password.
4. Click OK .

Password-protected projects are indicated by [IMAGE alt='' src=''] icon.

##### Updating project password

To update a project password

1. In the main menu, select Collaborate > Projects .
2. In the Manage Projects dialog, do one of the following:
  - Select a password-protected project and click [ATTACHMENT filename='set_password.png'] .
  - Right-click a password-protected project and click Set Password .
3. In the Update Password dialog, enter an old password, then enter and confirm a new password. [ATTACHMENT filename='update_password_dialog.png']
4. Click OK .

##### Removing project password

To remove a project password

1. In the main menu, select Collaborate > Projects .
2. In the Manage Projects dialog, do one of the following:
  - Select a password-protected project and click [ATTACHMENT filename='set_password.png'] .
  - Right-click a password-protected project and click Set Password .
3. In the Update Password dialog, enter an old password and leave the New Password and Confirm New Password boxes empty.
4. Click OK .

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=304015032 space=SYSML2CM version=1 -->
## PAGE 00014: (2026x Refresh1) Removing used projects

- page_id: `304015032`
- space_key: `SYSML2CM`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/SYSML2CM/pages/304015032/2026x+Refresh1+Removing+used+projects
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-04-29T17:17:40.944+02:00`
- ancestors: Versions of SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) Working with used projects
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

If you no longer need to use a project, you can remove it from the main projects via the Containment tree, or the **Project Usages** dialog.

Used projects are removed with all their references.

To remove a used project via the Containment tree

1. In the Containment tree of the main project, expand the Used Projects node.
2. Right-click a used project and select Remove . [ATTACHMENT filename='removing_used_projects.png']
3. When the question dialog opens, click Yes to confirm that you want to remove the used project.

Removing a used project via the **Project Usages** dialog

1. Open the Project Usages dialog:
  - In the main menu, select Options > Project Usages .
  - In the main menu, select Collaborate > Project Usages > Project Usages .
2. Do one of the following:
  - Select a used project and click [IMAGE alt='' src=''].
  - Right-click a used project and select Remove Used Project (with references) > Remove with References . [ATTACHMENT filename='removing_used_projects2.png']
3. When the question dialog opens, click Yes to confirm that you want to remove the used project.

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=304015084 space=SYSML2CM version=1 -->
## PAGE 00016: (2026x Refresh1) Reviewing project history

- page_id: `304015084`
- space_key: `SYSML2CM`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/SYSML2CM/pages/304015084/2026x+Refresh1+Reviewing+project+history
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-04-29T17:17:41.844+02:00`
- ancestors: Versions of SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation
- labels: ['history-dialog', 'out-of-sync', 'set-as-latest']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

The **History** dialog allows you to review project version history, including the author, commit time, and comment of each version. In addition, you can use the dialog to open a historical project version and set a historical version as the latest version of the project.

To review the project version history

1. In the main menu, select Collaborate > Projects .
2. In the Manage Project dialog, do one of the following:
  - Select a project and click [ATTACHMENT filename='project_history.png'] .
  - Right-click a project and select Project History .
3. In the **History** dialog, review the version list of the selected project or project branch. If a version has tags, you can see them next to the version number. 
 
[IMAGE alt='' src='']

##### Opening historical project versions

You can open a historical project version in a read-only mode.

To open a historical project version

1. In the main menu, select Collaborate > Projects .
2. In the Manage Project dialog, do one of the following:
  - Select a project and click [ATTACHMENT filename='project_history.png'] .
  - Right-click a project and select Project History .
3. In the **History** dialog, select the project version you want to open and click the **Open** button. 
 
[IMAGE alt='' src='']

##### Restoring historical project versions

You can restore a historical project version by setting it as the latest version of the project.

To restore a historical project version

1. In the main menu, select Collaborate > Projects .
2. In the Manage Project dialog, do one of the following:
  - Select a project and click [ATTACHMENT filename='project_history.png'] .
  - Right-click a project and select Project History .
3. In the **History** dialog, select the project version you want to restore (set as latest).
4. Do one of the following:
  - If you want to set the selected project version as the latest version of the open project or project branch, click the Set as Latest button.
  - If you want to set the selected project version as the latest version of another project branch (or trunk if a branch is open), click the arrow on the Set as Latest button and select Select Branch . Then select a project branch (or trunk) and click OK . [ATTACHMENT filename='restoring_historical_version.png']

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=304015019 space=SYSML2CM version=1 -->
## PAGE 00018: (2026x Refresh1) Single Sign-On Authentication

- page_id: `304015019`
- space_key: `SYSML2CM`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/SYSML2CM/pages/304015019/2026x+Refresh1+Single+Sign-On+Authentication
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-04-29T17:17:40.770+02:00`
- ancestors: Versions of SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) Starting a collaboration session
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

You can log in to Teamwork Cloud using single sign-on authentication (SSO). You can use the SAML authentication protocol (e.g., ForgeRock, Ping, WSO2), which means that:

- You do not need to enter your credentials each time you want to log in.
- A weak password or the need to update it is not an issue.

To log in to Teamwork Cloud using single sign-on authentication

1. In the main menu, select Collaborate > Login .
2. In the **Login** dialog, select the **Single Sign On** tab.
3. In the **Server** box, enter the server name (address). If you need to specify the server port, use the following format <server_name>:<port_number>. 
 
[IMAGE alt='' src='']
4. If you want the client application to remember your credentials and automatically log in to the server the next time you start, select the Auto Login to Server check box.
5. If you want to connect to the server using the SSL connection, select the **Use Secured Connection (SSL)** check box. The SSL connection must be established on both the server and the client side.
6. Click **OK**.
7. In the appropriate fields of the open dialog, enter your username and password.
8. Click the Sign in button. [ATTACHMENT filename='single_sign_on_login_dialog.png']

Wait until you are connected to the server, and then you can start performing collaborative tasks.

SSO implementation is based on the [JxBrowser platform](https://www.teamdev.com/jxbrowser), andis supported by following OS:

- Windows (32-bit & 64-bit)
  - Windows 10
  - Windows 8 & 8.1
  - Windows 7
  - Windows Server 2008 R2
  - Windows Server 2012
  - Windows Server 2016
- Linux (32-bit & 64-bit)
  - Ubuntu 12.04+
  - Debian 7.7+
  - Fedora 20
  - openSUSE 13.1
  - RedHat Enterprise Linux 7
- macOS (64-bit)
  - macOS 10.9.x - 10.12.x

For more information about supported OS, please refer to [JxBrowser system requirements](https://jxbrowser-support.teamdev.com/docs/guides/introduction/requirements.html).

##### Configuring SSO as the only login option

If you prefer to have only a Single Sign On login option, you can enable it by adding an argument to the properties file of the modeling tool:

1. Go to <modeling tool installation directory>/bin and open the properties file of your modeling tool.
2. In the JAVA_ARGS line, add the **-Dhide.login.tab=true****argument.
3. Restart the modeling tool.

**Related pages**

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Authentication server' space='MCS']

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=304015184 space=SYSML2CM version=1 -->
## PAGE 00019: (2026x Refresh1) Standard SysML v2 REST/HTTP API

- page_id: `304015184`
- space_key: `SYSML2CM`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/SYSML2CM/pages/304015184/2026x+Refresh1+Standard+SysML+v2+REST+HTTP+API
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-04-29T17:17:44.671+02:00`
- ancestors: Versions of SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) Server-side capabilities
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

This article provides information about standard SysML v2 REST/HTTP API service availability in Teamwork Cloud. It outlines the supported API service groups, upcoming services, and current limitations.

##### Supported API Service Groups

Teamwork Cloud supports all of the standard API service groups and their service mappings to HTTP/REST API PSM:

- Project Services
- Project Data Versioning Services (including Tag Services, Branch Services, Commit Services)
- Element Navigation Services
- Query Service
- External Relationship Service
- Project Usage Service

##### Query Service Settings

By default, Query Services work out of the box in Teamwork Cloud installation; however, it does not support queries containing derived properties or those expected to return derived property values.

To enable Query Services with derived properties, you need to index projects to be queried upfront using our Elasticsearch-based indexing engine.

##### Limitations

The following limitations apply to the supported services:

- Project Data Versioning Services -
  - The createCommit service does not currently allow changing a version of a used project.
  - The createCommit service requires specifying implied model relationships within the request payload when creating SysML v2 model elements to ensure the end model is semantically correct.

##### Accessing the SysML v2 REST/HTTP API

To access the SysML v2 REST API, go to*https://<server_IP>:8443/sysmlv2-api/swagger-ui/index.html*where **<server_IP>** is your Teamwork Cloud server IP.

## PAGE 00020: (2026x Refresh1) Starting a collaboration session

- page_id: `304014996`
- space_key: `SYSML2CM`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/SYSML2CM/pages/304014996/2026x+Refresh1+Starting+a+collaboration+session
- version_number: 2
- version_date: `2026-04-29T17:18:38.961+02:00`
- ancestors: Versions of SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

#### NOTE: Prerequisites

Prerequisites

To log in to Teamwork Cloud:

- You need to have a user account on the server. If an LDAP connection is set up , you can also log in with users imported from LDAP .
- The server must be running.

To log in to Teamwork Cloud

1. In the main menu, select Collaborate > Login . Single sign-on authenticationIf you want to use single sign-on authentication, follow the instructions provided [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='(2026x Refresh1) Single Sign-On Authentication' space=''].
2. In the **Login** tab of the open dialog, fill in the following boxes:
  - **User name** - enter your user name.
  - **Password** - enter the password for your user account.
  - **Server name** - enter the server name (address). If you need to specify the server port, use the following format <server_name>:<port_number>. 
 
[IMAGE alt='' src='']
3. If you want the client application to remember your credentials and automatically log in to the server the next time you start, select the Auto Login to Server check box.
4. If you want to connect to the server using the SSL connection, select the **Use Secured Connection (SSL)** check box. The SSL connection must be established on both the server and the client side.
5. Click **OK**.

Wait until you are connected to the server, and then you can start performing collaborative tasks.

To log out of Teamwork Cloud

- In the main menu, select Collaborate > Logout .

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=304014987 space=SYSML2CM version=1 -->
## PAGE 00021: (2026x Refresh1) SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation

- page_id: `304014987`
- space_key: `SYSML2CM`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/SYSML2CM/pages/304014987/2026x+Refresh1+SysML+v2+Collaborative+Modeling+Documentation
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-04-29T17:17:40.378+02:00`
- ancestors: Versions of SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

lightgrey

This guide provides documentation for client-side collaboration on SysML v2 server projects.

Collaborative modeling allows multiple users to work on different parts of the same server project, ensuring efficient teamwork and real-time collaboration. The collaborative modeling documentation explains the principles of working with server projects stored on Teamwork Cloud.

Teamwork Cloud provides a repository for storing projects and users, allows managing user permissions, and offers the same solutions and user experience for working with server projects.

##### Basic concepts

Before you start working with server projects, get acquainted with the following collaborative modeling concepts.

| Concept | Description |
| --- | --- |
| Server project | A project stored either in Teamwork Cloud or on the 3DEXPERIENCE platform. |
| User | A person who can log in to Teamwork Cloud or the 3DEXPERIENCE platform and has permissions to access one or more server projects. |
| Version | The smallest possible milestone of the project development in Teamwork Cloud. A new project version is created each time a user commits project changes to the server. Versions are labeled by numbers in ascending order starting from 1 (one). |
| Branch | A copy of a server project made at a certain point of the project development. Each project branch can be developed independently. |
| Trunk | The base branch of a server project that cannot be deleted. Project branches are usually created from the trunk. |
| Comment | An optional description of a project version/iteration made during the project commit. |
| Tag | A label of a project version/iteration helping to identify it from other project versions/iterations. |
| Commit | A process of sending the changes made in the project to the server. Each commit creates a new project version/iteration. |
| Author | A user who has committed a particular project version/iteration. |
| Update | A process of loading the latest project version/iteration to the modeling tool. |
| Category | A concept for grouping projects in a server repository. |
| Used project/project usage | A server project used in the project you are working with. It can be a library, profile, or regular project. |

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=304015103 space=SYSML2CM version=1 -->
## PAGE 00022: (2026x Refresh1) Updating changes from the server

- page_id: `304015103`
- space_key: `SYSML2CM`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/SYSML2CM/pages/304015103/2026x+Refresh1+Updating+changes+from+the+server
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-04-29T17:17:42.274+02:00`
- ancestors: Versions of SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

##### Updating projects from the server

It is recommended to update a server project when a new project version is available on the server. During project update, the local project changes are merged with the changes committed to the server by other people.

To update a project from the server

- Do one of the following:
  - In the main menu, select **Collaborate** > **Update Project**.
  - Press Ctrl+U.

##### Conflict resolution

It is important to understand how conflicts are resolved during project updates when several users work with the same project simultaneously. If a conflict occurs while updating a server project, it is resolved the following way:

- If two users modify the same element attribute or diagram, your local changes win over the changes committed to the server.
- If someone deletes the element you are modifying locally, your local changes of that element are lost (the element is deleted).
- If two users modify or create a relationship, both of the relationships are kept after the project update. In this case you have to decide which relationship to keep, otherwise the model may become invalid. ExamplesSince SysML v2 is based on relationships, the type of conflict where an additional relationship is created is the most common. Here are several examples:If two users specify the value of the same attribute, e.g., a = 5 (created by user 1) and a = 3 (created by user 2), two relationships are created to values 5 and 3. After the update, user 2 would have to decide which value he wants to keep.If two users set the type of the same part, e.g., user 1 sets the type to 'A' and user 2 sets the type to 'B', both types of the part are kept - 'A' and 'B. Again, user 2 has to decide which type to keep.

##### Notifications about new project versions

When several users work on the same project simultaneously, you will be notified if new changes are committed to the server project you are working on.

To turn notifications about new project versions on/off

1. In the main menu, select Options > Environment .
2. In the Environment Options dialog, select the Collaboration option group.
3. Find the Notify About New Project Versions on the Server property. Do one of the following:

- 
  - Set the property to true to get notifications about new project versions.
  - Set the property to false to turn the notifications about new project versions off.

You can specify the interval you want the modeling tool to check for new project versions on the server. By default, this time interval is two minutes.

To specify the time interval to check for new project versions

1. In the main menu, select Options > Environment .
2. In the Environment Options dialog, select the Collaboration option group.
3. Specify the Interval to Check For New Project Version (in seconds) property.

Any changes to theinterval will be applied to newly opened projects only.

If notifications are turned on, the modeling tool will automatically check and notify you when a new project version is available on the server.

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

````html
<h3>Updating projects from the server</h3><p><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">It is recommended to update a server project when a new project version is available on the server. During project update, the local project changes are merged with the changes committed to the server by other people</span><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">.</span></p><p><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);"> </span></p><p><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">To update a project from the server</span></p><hr /><ul><li><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">Do one of the following:</span><ul><li><p><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">In the main menu, select <strong>Collaborate</strong> &gt; <strong>Update Project</strong>.</span></p></li><li><p><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#333333);">Press Ctrl+U.</span></p></li></ul></li></ul><h3>Conflict resolution</h3><p><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#172b4d);"><span> I</span>t is important to understand how conflicts are resolved during project updates when several users work with the same project simultaneously. If a conflict occurs while updating a server project, it is resolved the following way:</span></p><ul style="text-align: left;"><li>If two users modify the same element attribute or diagram, your local changes win over the changes committed to the server.</li><li>If someone deletes the element you are modifying locally, your local changes of that element are lost (the element is deleted).</li><li>If two users modify or create a relationship, both of the relationships are kept after the project update. In this case you have to decide which relationship to keep, otherwise the model may become invalid.<br /><ac:structured-macro ac:name="tip" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="9acb2d1f-64b6-47e2-a6fa-93c307af5624"><ac:parameter ac:name="title">Examples</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p><span style="color:var(--ds-text,#172b4d);">Since SysML v2 is based on relationships, the type of conflict where an additional relationship is created is the most common. Here are several examples:</span></p><ul><li>If two users specify the value of the same attribute, e.g., a = 5 (created by user 1) and a = 3 (created by user 2), two relationships are created to values 5 and 3. After the update, user 2 would have to decide which value he wants to keep.</li><li>If two users set the type of the same part, e.g., user 1 sets the type to 'A' and user 2 sets the type to 'B', both types of the part are kept - 'A' and 'B. Again, user 2 has to decide which type to keep.</li></ul></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></li></ul><h3>Notifications about new project versions</h3><p>When several users work on the same project simultaneously, you will be notified if new changes are committed to the server project you are working on. </p><p><br /></p><p>To turn notifications about new project versions on/off</p><hr /><ol><li>In the main menu, select <strong>Options</strong> &gt; <strong>Environment</strong>.</li><li>In the <strong>Environment Options </strong>dialog, select the <strong>Collaboration</strong> option group.</li><li><span>Find the </span><strong>Notify About New Project Versions on the Server</strong> property.<span> Do one of the following: </span></li></ol><ul><li style="list-style-type: none;background-image: none;"><ul><li>Set the property to <em>true</em> to get notifications about new project versions.</li><li>Set the property to <em>false</em> to turn the notifications about new project versions off.</li></ul></li></ul><p><br /></p><p>You can specify the interval you want the modeling tool to check for new project versions on the server. By default, this time interval is two minutes. </p><p><br /></p><p>To specify the time interval to check for new project versions</p><hr /><ol><li>In the main menu, select <strong>Options</strong> &gt; <strong>Environment</strong>.</li><li>In the <strong>Environment Options </strong>dialog, select the <strong>Collaboration</strong> option group.</li><li>Specify the <strong>Interval to Check For New Project Version (in seconds) </strong>property.   <br /><br /></li></ol><ac:structured-macro ac:name="info" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="fa9f1995-91e4-45f2-9111-d0e895d37910"><ac:rich-text-body><p>Any changes to the<span> </span>interval will be applied to newly opened projects only.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><p class="auto-cursor-target"><span style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">If notifications are turned on, the modeling tool will automatically check and notify you when a new project version is available on the server.</span></p>
````

## PAGE 00023: (2026x Refresh1) Using server projects

- page_id: `304015041`
- space_key: `SYSML2CM`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/SYSML2CM/pages/304015041/2026x+Refresh1+Using+server+projects
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-04-29T17:17:41.105+02:00`
- ancestors: Versions of SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) Working with used projects
- labels: ['indirectly-used-project', 'directly-used-project', 'unrestored-unknown-attachment']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

To use a project in another project, you must have the Administer Resources permission.

To use a server project in another server project

1. Open the Project Usages dialog:
  - In the main menu, select Options > Project Usages .
  - In the main menu, select Collaborate > Project Usages > Project Usages .
2. Click [ATTACHMENT filename='use_server_project.png'] .
3. In the Use Server Project dialog, select the project you want to use and click Next . [ATTACHMENT filename='using_server_project.png']
4. Select the project version you want to use and click the **Finish** button. 
 
[IMAGE alt='' src='']

Used projects are displayed under the Used Projects node in the Containment tree and in the **Project Usages** dialog.

## PAGE 00024: (2026x Refresh1) Viewing Version Properties

- page_id: `304015133`
- space_key: `SYSML2CM`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/SYSML2CM/pages/304015133/2026x+Refresh1+Viewing+Version+Properties
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-04-29T17:17:42.829+02:00`
- ancestors: Versions of SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) Managing server projects
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

The **Version Properties** dialog shows project version information, such as comments, tags, used projects, and meta information.

To view version properties

1. In the main menu, select Collaborate > Projects .
2. In the Manage Projects dialog, do one of the following:
  - Select a project and click [ATTACHMENT filename='version_properties.png'] .
  - Right-click a project and select Version Properties .
3. In the Version Properties dialog, do the following:
  - View the project version, author, and creation date. 
 
[IMAGE alt='' src='']
  - In the **Comment** tab, view the commit comment for the project version. 
 
[IMAGE alt='' src='']
  - In the **Tags** tab, view project version tags. 
 
[IMAGE alt='' src='']
  - In the **Used Projects** tab, view project usages.
  - In the **Meta information** tab, see which programs and plugins are required to open the project. 
 
[IMAGE alt='' src='']

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=304015095 space=SYSML2CM version=1 -->
## PAGE 00025: (2026x Refresh1) Working with change sets

- page_id: `304015095`
- space_key: `SYSML2CM`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/SYSML2CM/pages/304015095/2026x+Refresh1+Working+with+change+sets
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-04-29T17:17:42.093+02:00`
- ancestors: Versions of SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation
- labels: ['unrestored-unknown-attachment']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

When editing a server project, you can track local project changes in the **Change Sets**panel. A change set is a related group of element, diagram, and symbol modifications in a project created locally and not yet committed to the server. You may have several change sets in your project and commit them one by one. You can suspend one change set, commit another change set, and then resume your workon the previously suspended change set.

To open the Change Sets panel

- In the main menu, select **Window** > **Change Sets**.

###### [IMAGE alt='' src='']The Change Sets panel.

##### Managing change sets

You can create as many change sets as you need. Only one change set can be active at a time. For a new change set to be created, all other change sets must be suspended. To identify change sets, you can rename them.

To manage an *active* change set

- Right-click an active change set and select one of the following commands:
  - Commit - to commit local changes to the server.
  - Rename - to modify the name of the change set.
  - Suspend - to suspend the change set. When you suspend a change set, a new change set is created for further model changes. Suspended change sets cannot be committed to the server.
  - Discard - to discard local changes in the change set. After discarding a change set, all its changes are removed from the model. This action cannot be undone.
  - Tag version with Change ID after Commit - for the Change ID to be automatically reflected in the Project History after committing the project.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### Managing an active change set.

To manage a *suspended* change set

- Right-click a suspended change set and select one of the following commands:
  - Resume - to resume work with a suspended change set. Ensure that the active change set is suspended before resuming work with a suspended change set.
  - Discard - to discard local changes in the change set. After discarding a change set, all its changes are removed from the model. This action cannot be undone.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### Managing a suspended change set.

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=304015023 space=SYSML2CM version=1 -->
## PAGE 00026: (2026x Refresh1) Working with used projects

- page_id: `304015023`
- space_key: `SYSML2CM`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/SYSML2CM/pages/304015023/2026x+Refresh1+Working+with+used+projects
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-04-29T17:17:40.842+02:00`
- ancestors: Versions of SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x Refresh1) SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

To manage Teamwork Cloud project usages, you must have the Administer Resources permission.

When a server project has weakly dependent parts, such as type libraries or models of different phases of system development, it is recommended to use project partitioning. Project partitioning means that parts of a model are moved to separate projects, which can be reused in other projects. The projects used in other projects are referred to as *used projects* or *project usages*. Used projects are read-only, so you cannot modify them directly from the main project. To modify a used project, you need to open it as a stand-alone.

To learn more about project usages, see the following topics:

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

````html
<ac:structured-macro ac:name="note" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="660e2072-9c67-4bfd-a314-4d8ce037351b"><ac:rich-text-body><p>To manage Teamwork Cloud project usages, you must have the Administer Resources permission.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><p>When a server project has weakly dependent parts, such as type libraries or models of different phases of system development, it is recommended to use project partitioning. Project partitioning means that parts of a model are moved to separate projects, which can be reused in other projects. The projects used in other projects are referred to as <em>used projects</em> or <em>project usages</em>. Used projects are read-only, so you cannot modify them directly from the main project. To modify a used project, you need to open it as a stand-alone.</p><p>To learn more about project usages, see the following topics:</p><p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="children" ac:schema-version="2" ac:macro-id="74aca093-b216-4ef1-a87f-e55bbe63c2da" /></p>
````

## PAGE 00027: (2026x) Adding projects to the server

- page_id: `286557030`
- space_key: `SYSML2CM`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/SYSML2CM/pages/286557030/2026x+Adding+projects+to+the+server
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-01-26T12:47:14.118+01:00`
- ancestors: Versions of SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x) SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

#### NOTE: Prerequisites

Prerequisites

To add projects to the server, you must have the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Permissions' space='MCS'] or the Resource Creator role for the category in which you want to store projects.

You can add projects to the server in one of the following ways:

- 
- 

##### Creating server projects

To create a server project

1. Do one of the following to open the New Server Project dialog:
  - In the main menu, select Collaborate > New Server Project .
  - In the main menu, select Collaborate > Projects and click the New button. [ATTACHMENT filename='new_server_project.png']
2. On the left side of the dialog, select the SysML v2 Project type.
3. In the Name box, enter the project name.
4. Optionally, click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] next to the **Category**box, and select the category where you want to store your project. To create a new category for the project, click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] in the **Select Category** dialog.
5. Click OK .

##### Importing local projects to the server

To import a local project to the server

1. Open the project you want to add to the server from the local repository.
2. In the main menu, select Collaborate > Add Project to Server . Only projects saved as new versions can be added to the server. If your local project is saved as a draft, you will be prompted to save it as a new version before proceeding to the next step. For more information, see the *Saving local projects* section on page [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Managing local projects' space='SYSML2P']
3. In the Import Project to the Server dialog, review the actions that will be performed on the main project and any used projects. [ATTACHMENT filename='import_project_to_server_dialog.png']
4. Optionally, click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] next to the **Category**box, and select the category where you want to store your project. To create a new category for the project, click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] in the **Select Category** dialog. Click the Import button.

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=286557045 space=SYSML2CM version=1 -->
## PAGE 00028: (2026x) Branching projects

- page_id: `286557045`
- space_key: `SYSML2CM`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/SYSML2CM/pages/286557045/2026x+Branching+projects
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2026-01-26T12:47:14.363+01:00`
- ancestors: Versions of SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x) SysML v2 Collaborative Modeling Documentation > (2026x) Managing server projects
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

Creating a project branch duplicates a specific project version and enables users to work on the project simultaneously. Branching increases productivity if several development teams are working on a single product. Branches can be created from any version/iteration of a project or its branch. The branch holds the information about the project version/iteration it is derived from.

#### NOTE: Permissions

Permissions

To create, remove, rename, archive, or unarchive a branch in Teamwork Cloud, you must have the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Permissions' space='MCS'].

##### Creating project branches

To create a project branch

1. In the main menu, select Collaborate > Projects .
2. In the Manage Projects dialog, select the project you want to branch and click [ATTACHMENT filename='select_branch.png'] .
3. In the Select Branch dialog, click the Edit Branches button.
4. In the Edit Branches dialog, select the project version/iteration you want to branch and click the Create Branch button. [ATTACHMENT filename='edit_branches_dialog.png']
5. In the Branch name box of the open dialog, enter the branch name.
6. In the Comment box, optionally enter the branch description.
7. (For Teamwork Cloud only). If you want to branch project usages together with the main project, select the Branch used projects check box. [ATTACHMENT filename='create_branch_dialog.png']
8. Click OK . A new branch is created and displayed in the Edit Branches dialog. [ATTACHMENT filename='displaying_created_branch.png']

##### Opening project branches

To open a project branch

1. In the main menu, select Collaborate > Projects .
2. In the Manage Projects dialog, select the project whose branch you want to open and click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] .
3. In the **Select Branch** dialog, select the desired project branch and click **OK**. You can see the selected branch in the **Branch** column of the **Manage Projects** dialog.
4. Click the Open button to open the project branch.

The selected branch is displayed in the **Manage Projects** dialog. The branch name is displayed in the **Branch** column and you can open it as any other project.

##### Archiving project branches

You can hide the project branches that you do not work with anymore and maintain only for historical purposes.

To archive a project branch

1. In the main menu, select Collaborate > Projects .
2. In the Manage Projects dialog, s elect the project whose branch you want to archive and click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] .
3. In the Select Branch dialog, click the Edit Branches button.
4. In the Edit Branches dialog, r ight-click the branch you want to archive and select **Mark as Archived**. 
**[IMAGE alt='' src='']**

By default, archived branches are hidden in the project version tree.

- To show/hide archived branches, click [ATTACHMENT filename='options_button.png'] in the Edit Branches or Select Branch dialog and select or deselect the Show Archived Branches command.
- To unarchive an archived branch, right-click the archived branch in the Edit Branches dialog and deselect the **Mark as Archived** command.

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE
